# Fault Localization: ACPI Video Backlight Control Failure

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/linux--55b2af1c (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/linux--55b2af1c (mirror of torvalds/linux)
- **Kernel Version**: 5.6.7
- **Difficulty**: expert
- **Category**: fault_localization
- **Subsystem**: ACPI
- **Component**: Video/Backlight

## Bug Report

**Bug ID**: 207835
**Summary**: ACPI video backlight brightness control does not work on Acer TravelMate 5735Z by default

On the Intel GM45/GMA 4500MHD laptop with Debian Sid/unstable and Linux 5.6.7 and GNOME Shell 3.36.2, trying to change the brightness of the internal display using the function keys, GNOME shows the OSD, which seems to have five levels (from acer_wmi?), but the actual brightness does *not* change. There is only `/sys/class/backlight/intel_backlight/brightness` though, and writing values to it seems to work.

Booting the system with `acpi_backlight=vendor`, exposes `/sys/devices/platform/acer-wmi/backlight/acer-wmi/brightness`, but the behavior is the same.

Booting the system with `acpi_backlight=native` or `acpi_backlight=native`, changing the brightness with the function keys works, and there now seem to be 15 (or 16) levels.

```
$ grep '.*' /sys/class/dmi/id/*_* 2> /dev/null
/sys/class/dmi/id/bios_date:07/26/2011
/sys/class/dmi/id/bios_vendor:Acer
/sys/class/dmi/id/bios_version:V1.14
/sys/class/dmi/id/board_asset_tag:Base Board Asset Tag
/sys/class/dmi/id/board_name:BA51_MV
/sys/class/dmi/id/board_vendor:Acer
/sys/class/dmi/id/board_version:V1.14
/sys/class/dmi/id/chassis_asset_tag:
/sys/class/dmi/id/chassis_type:10
/sys/class/dmi/id/chassis_vendor:Acer
/sys/class/dmi/id/chassis_version:V1.14
/sys/class/dmi/id/product_family:Intel_Mobile
/sys/class/dmi/id/product_name:TravelMate 5735Z
/sys/class/dmi/id/product_sku:Montevina_Fab
/sys/class/dmi/id/product_version:V1.14
/sys/class/dmi/id/sys_vendor:Acer
```

82-assistanttext-
## Summary

I have successfully completed the fault localization task for the ACPI video backlight control failure on the Acer TravelMate 5735Z. Here's my analysis:

### Key Findings:

**Problem Identified:**
- The Acer TravelMate 5735Z (Intel GM45/GMA 4500MHD) has non-functional ACPI backlight brightness control in Linux 5.6.7 by default
- GNOME shows brightness controls but they don't work
- Writing to `/sys/class/backlight/intel_backlight/brightness` directly works, but function keys fail
- With `acpi_backlight=native` kernel parameter, brightness control works properly with 15-16 levels

**Root Cause:**
The device is missing from the `video_detect_dmi_table` in `drivers/acpi/video_detect.c`. By default, the system detects ACPI_VIDEO_BACKLIGHT capability and selects `acpi_backlight_video` as the backlight interface type. However, the ACPI video backlight driver doesn't work correctly on this particular hardware, while the native Intel backlight driver works perfectly.

**Fault Localization Results:**
- **Buggy File:** `drivers/acpi/video_detect.c`
- **Buggy Function/Data Structure:** `video_detect_dmi_table`
- **Confidence:** 0.85
- **Fix Required:** Add a DMI matching entry for Acer TravelMate 5735Z to force `acpi_backlight_native`

The results have been written to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`

By default, the system detects ACPI_VIDEO_BACKLIGHT capability and selects acpi_backlight_video as the backlight type, but the ACPI video backlight driver does not work correctly on this hardware. The bug report confirms that with acpi_backlight=native (which forces the native Intel backlight driver), brightness control works properly with 15-16 levels. Without this override, brightness control fails despite the native backlight interface (intel_backlight) being available.         Code Changes (1)
        
1. WRITE /workspace/fault_localization_result.json
{
  "buggy_files": ["drivers/acpi/video_detect.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["video_detect_dmi_table"],
  "confidence": 0.85,
  "reasoning": "The Acer TravelMate 5735Z with Intel GM45 chipset is missing from the video_detect_dmi_table. By default, the system detects ACPI_VIDEO_BACKLIGHT capability and selects acpi_backlight_video as the backlight type, but the ACPI video backlight driver does not work correctly on this hardware. The bug report confirms that with acpi_backlight=native (which forces the native Intel backlight driver), brightness control works properly with 15-16 levels. Without this override, brightness control fails despite the native backlight interface (intel_backlight) being available. The fix is to add a DMI quirk entry for this specific device model to force the use of acpi_backlight_native, allowing the working native backlight driver to be used instead of the broken ACPI video interface."
}
